## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Write Unit Tests for Bazel Starlark Rule Evaluation

## Objective
Write comprehensive unit tests for the Starlark evaluation of rule() calls in BUILD files, covering rule instantiation, attribute validation, and error handling.

## Steps
1. Study the Starlark rule evaluation in `src/main/java/com/google/devtools/build/lib/packages/`
2. Understand how `RuleClass` and `RuleFactory` process rule() calls
3. Study existing tests in `src/test/java/com/google/devtools/build/lib/packages/`
4. Create a test file `StarlarkRuleEvalTest.java` in the test directory with tests for:
   - Basic rule instantiation with required attributes
   - Missing required attribute produces error
   - Attribute type validation (string vs list vs label)
   - Default attribute values are applied
   - Visibility attribute handling
   - Rule name validation (valid and invalid names)

## Key Reference Files
- `src/main/java/com/google/devtools/build/lib/packages/RuleClass.java`
- `src/main/java/com/google/devtools/build/lib/packages/RuleFactory.java`
- `src/test/java/com/google/devtools/build/lib/packages/` — existing tests

## Success Criteria
- Test file exists in the test directory
- Tests cover rule instantiation
- Tests cover attribute validation
- Tests cover error cases

The test file is created correctly at `/workspace/src/test/java/com/google/devtools/build/lib/packages/StarlarkRuleEvalTest.java`.

Here's a summary of what was implemented:

## StarlarkRuleEvalTest.java

The test class extends `PackageLoadingTestCase` and follows the same patterns used in `PackageFactoryTest.java` and `RuleTest.java`.

### Setup
- `@Before setUpCustomRule()` creates a custom Starlark rule `my_rule` in `rules/my_rule.bzl` with four attributes:
  - `srcs`: optional `label_list`
  - `out`: **mandatory** `string`
  - `deps`: optional `label_list`
  - `num`: optional `int` with default `42`

### Tests

| Test | Coverage |
|------|----------|
| `testBasicRuleInstantiation` | Rule instantiation with mandatory attr — verifies name, rule class, and no errors |
| `testMissingRequiredAttributeProducesError` | Missing mandatory `out` attr — verifies error message `"missing value for mandatory attribute 'out' in 'my_rule' rule"` |
| `testAttributeTypeValidation` | Passing a list `["not_a_string"]` to a string attribute — verifies `"expected value of type 'string'"` error |
| `testDefaultAttributeValuesApplied` | Verifies `num` defaults to `StarlarkInt.of(42)` and `srcs` defaults to empty list |
| `testVisibilityAttributeHandling` | Sets `visibility = ["//visibility:public"]` and verifies `RuleVisibility.PUBLIC_LABEL` in declared labels |
| `testValidRuleName` | A rule named `valid_rule_name` loads without errors |
| `testInvalidRuleName` | A rule named `invalid:name` produces `"target names may not contain ':'"` error |

### Key implementation notes
- Error messages are verified against the actual source code in `RuleClass.java` (line 2338) and `BuildType.java` (`AttributeConversionContext.toString()`)
- `loadPackage()` follows the exact same pattern as `PackageFac

<p>Type symbols are primarily used for their <code>convert</code> method, which is a kind of cast\\n47:  * operator enabling conversion from untyped (Object) references to values in the build language, to\\n48:  * typed references.\\n49:  *\\n50:  * <p>For example, this code type-converts a value <code>x</code> returned by the evaluator, to a\\n51:  * list of strings:\\n52:  *\\n53:  * <pre>\\n54:  *  Object x = expr.eval(env);\\n55:  *  List&lt;String&gt; s = Type.STRING_LIST.convert(x);\\n56:  *  </pre>\\n57:  *\\n58:  * <p><b>BEFORE YOU ADD A NEW TYPE:</b>\\n59:  *\\n60:  * <p>We frequently get requests to create a new kind of attribute type whenever a use case doesn't\\n61:  * seem to fit into one of the existing types. This is almost always a bad idea. The most complex\\n62:  * type we currently have is probably STRING_LIST_DICT or maybe LABEL_KEYED_STRING_DICT. But no\\n63:  * matter what you support, someone will always want to add another layer of structure. It's even\\n64:  * been suggested to allow JSON or arbitrary Starlark values in attributes.\\n65:  *\\n66:  * <p>Adding a new type has implications for many different systems. The whole of the loading phase\\n67:  * needs to know about the type -- how to serialize it, how to format it for `bazel query`, how to\\n68:  * traverse label dependencies embedded within it. Then you need to think about how to represent\\n69:  * attribute values of that type in Starlark within a rule implementation function, and come up with\\n70:  * a good name for that type in the Starlark `attr` module. All of the tooling for formatting,\\n71:  * linting, and analyzing BUILD files may need to be updated.\\n72:  *\\n73:  * <p>It's usually possible to accomplish the end goal without making the target attribute grammar\\n74:  * more expressive. If it's not, that may be a sign that attributes are not the right mechanism to\\n75:  * use, and perhaps instead you should use opaque string identifiers, or labels to sub-targets with\\n76:  * more structure (think toolchains, platforms, config_setting).\\n77:  *\\n78:  * <p>Any new attribute type should be general-purpose and meet a high bar of usefulness (unlikely\\n79:  * since we seem to be doing fine so far without it), and not overly complicate BUILD files or rule\\n80:  * implementation functions.\\n81:  */\\n82: // TODO(adonovan): update documentation here and elsewhere to use the term\\n83: // \\\"rule attribute values\\\" or \\\"valid attribute types\\\" where appropriate,\\n84: // and not \\\"value in the build language\\\", which is a much broader set of\\n85: // possible Starlark values. Root of Type symbol hierarchy for values in the build language.\n45:  *\n46:  * <p>Type symbols are primarily used for their <code>convert</code> method, which is a kind of cast\n47:  * operator enabling conversion from untyped (Object) references to values in the build language, to\n48:  * typed references.\n49:  *\n50:  * <p>For example, this code type-converts a value <code>x</code> returned by the evaluator, to a\n51:  * list of strings:\n52:  *\n53:  * <pre>\n54:  *  Object x = expr.eval(env);\n55:  *  List&lt;String&gt; s = Type.STRING_LIST.convert(x);\n56:  *  </pre>\n57:  *\n58:  * <p><b>BEFORE YOU ADD A NEW TYPE:</b>\n59:  *\n60:  * <p>We frequently get requests to create a new kind of attribute type whenever a use case doesn't\n61:  * seem to fit into one of the existing types. This is almost always a bad idea. The most complex\n62:  * type we currently have is probably STRING_LIST_DICT or maybe LABEL_KEYED_STRING_DICT. But no\n63:  * matter what you support, someone will always want to add another layer of structure. It's even\n64:  * been suggested to allow JSON or arbitrary Starlark values in attributes.\n65:  *\n66:  * <p>Adding a new type has implications for many different systems. The whole of the loading phase\n67:  * needs to know about the type -- how to serialize it, how to format it for `bazel query`, how to\n68:  * traverse label dependencies embedded within it. Then you need to think about how to represent\n69:  * attribute values of that type in Starlark within a rule implementation function, and come up with\n70:  * a good name for that type in the Starlark `attr` module. All of the tooling for formatting,\n71:  * linting, and analyzing BUILD files may need to be updated.\n72:  *\n73:  * <p>It's usually possible to accomplish the end goal without making the target attribute grammar\n74:  * more expressive. If it's not, that may be a sign that attributes are not the right mechanism to\n75:  * use, and perhaps instead you should use opaque string identifiers, or labels to sub-targets with\n76:  * more structure (think toolchains, platforms, config_setting).\n77:  *\n78:  * <p>Any new attribute type should be general-purpose and meet a high bar of usefulness (unlikely\n79:  * since we seem to be doing fine so far without it), and not overly complicate BUILD files or rule\n80:  * implementation functions.\n81:  */\n82: // TODO(adonovan): update documentation here and elsewhere to use the term\n83: // \"rule attribute values\" or \"valid attribute types\" where appropriate,\n84: // and not \"value in the build language\", which is a much broader set of\n85: // possible Starlark values. Also link to the canonical set of valid attribute\n86: // types, both Starlark and native.\n87: public abstract class Type<T> {\n88: \n89:   Type() {}\n90: \n91:   /**\n92:    * Converts a legal Starlark value x into an Java value of type T.\n93:    *\n94:    * <p>x must be directly convertible to this type. To handle those expressions, see {@link\n97:    * com.google.devtools.build.lib.packages.BuildType#convertFromBuildLangType}.\n98:    *\n99:    * @param x The Starlark value to convert.\n100:    * @param what An object whose toString method returns a description of the purpose of x.\n101: ",

This does create a tight coupling to the implementation, but this\n2367:         // is unavoidable since licenses are no longer a first-class type but we want first class\n2368:         // behavior in Bazel core.\n2369:         //\n2370:         // A different approach that would not depend on the implementation of the rule could filter\n2371:         // the list of default_applicable_metadata and not include the metadata rule if it matches\n2372:         // the name of the current rule. This obviously fixes the self-assignment rule, but the\n2373:         // resulting graph is semantically strange. The interpretation of the graph would be that\n2374:         // the metadata rule is subject to the metadata of the *other* default metadata, but not\n2375:         // itself. That looks very odd, and it's not semantically accurate.\n2376:         // As an alternate, if the self-edge is detected, why not simply drop all the\n2377:         // default_applicable_metadata attributes and avoid this oddness? That would work and\n2378:         // fix the self-edge problem, but for nodes that don't have the self-edge problem, they\n2379:         // would get all default_applicable_metadata and now the graph is inconsistent in that some\n2380:         // license() rules have applicable_metadata while others do not.\n2381: ",
    "url": "https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/bazel--8.0.0@12f256c9dffb17d03d47b3f06bf34f67c976e4aa/-/blob/src/main/java/com/google/devtools/build/lib/packages/RuleClass.java%3FL2280-2380"
  }
}

com.google.devtools.build.lib.packages.util.PackageLoadingTestCase;\nimport net.starlark.java.eval.StarlarkInt;\nimport org.junit.Before;\nimport org.junit.Test;\nimport org.junit.runner.RunWith;\nimport org.junit.runners.JUnit4;\n\n/**\n * Unit tests for Starlark rule evaluation in BUILD files, covering rule instantiation, attribute\n * validation, and error handling.\n */\n@RunWith(JUnit4.class)\npublic final class StarlarkRuleEvalTest extends PackageLoadingTestCase {\n\n  @Before\n  public void setUpCustomRule() throws Exception {\n    scratch.file(\"rules/BUILD\");\n    scratch.file(\n        \"rules/my_rule.bzl\",\n        \"\"\"\n        def _impl(ctx):\n            pass\n\n        my_rule = rule(\n            implementation = _impl,\n            attrs = {\n                \"srcs\": attr.label_list(allow_files = True),\n                \"out\": attr.string(mandatory = True),\n                \"deps\": attr.label_list(),\n                \"num\": attr.int(default = 42),\n            },\n        )\n        \"\"\");\n  }\n\n  private Package loadPackage(String pkgid) throws Exception {\n    return getTarget(\"//\" + pkgid + \":BUILD\").getPackage();\n  }\n\n  /** Test 1: Basic rule instantiation with required attributes. */\n  @Test\n  public void testBasicRuleInstantiation() throws Exception {\n    scratch.file(\n        \"pkg/BUILD\",\n        \"\"\"\n        load(\"//rules:my_rule.bzl\", \"my_rule\")\n\n        my_rule(\n            name = \"my_target\",\n            out = \"output.txt\",\n        )\n        \"\"\");\n\n    Rule rule = (Rule) getTarget(\"//pkg:my_target\");\n    assertThat(rule).isNotNull();\n    assertThat(rule.getName()).isEqualTo(\"my_target\");\n    assertThat(rule.getRuleClass()).isEqualTo(\"my_rule\");\n    assertThat(rule.containsErrors()).isFalse();\n  }\n\n  /** Test 2: Missing required attribute produces an error. */\n  @Test\n  public void testMissingRequiredAttributeProducesError() throws Exception {\n    reporter.removeHandler(failFastHandler);\n    scratch.file(\n        \"pkg/BUILD\",\n        \"\"\"\n        load(\"//rules:my_rule.bzl\", \"my_rule\")\n\n        my_rule(name = \"my_target\")\n        \"\"\");\n\n    Package pkg = loadPackage(\"pkg\");\n    assertThat(pkg.containsErrors()).isTrue();\n    assertContainsEvent(\"missing value for mandatory attribute 'out' in 'my_rule' rule\");\n  }\n\n  /** Test 3: Attribute type validation \u2014 passing a list where a string is expected. */\n  @Test\n  public void testAttributeTypeValidation() throws Exception {\n    reporter.removeHandler(failFastHandler);\n    scratch.file(\n        \"pkg/BUILD\",\n        \"\"\"\n        load(\"//rules:my_rule.bzl\", \"my_rule\")\n\n        my_rule(\n            name = \"my_target\",\n            out = [\"not_a_string\"],\n        )\n        \"\"\");\n\n    Package pkg = loadPackage(\"pkg\");\n    assertThat(pkg.containsErrors()).isTrue();\n    assertContainsEvent(\"expected value of type 'string'\");\n  }\n\n  /** Test 4: Default attribute values are applied when not specified. */\n  @Test\n  public void testDefaultAttributeValuesApplied() throws Exception {\n    scratch.file(\n        \"pkg/BUILD\",\n        \"\"\"\n        load(\"//rules:my_rule.bzl\", \"my_rule\")\n\n        my_rule(\n            name = \"my_target\",\n            out = \"output.txt\",\n        )\n        \"\"\");\n\n    Rule rule = (Rule) getTarget(\"//pkg:my_target\");\n    assertThat(rule.containsErrors()).isFalse();\n\n    AttributeMap attrs = RawAttributeMapper.of(rule);\n    assertThat(attrs.get(\"num\", Type.INTEGER)).isEqualTo(StarlarkInt.of(42));\n    assertThat(attrs.get(\"srcs\", BuildType.LABEL_LIST)).isEmpty();\n  }\n\n  /** Test 5: Visibility attribute can be set and is reflected in the rule. */\n  @Test\n  public void testVisibilityAttributeHandling() throws Exception {\n    scratch.file(\n        \"pkg/BUILD\",\n        \"\"\"\n        load(\"//rules:my_rule.bzl\", \"my_rule\")\n\n        my_rule(\n            name = \"my_public_target\",\n            out = \"output.txt\",\n            visibility = [\"//visibility:public\"],\n        )\n        \"\"\");\n\n    Rule rule = (Rule) getTarget(\"//pkg:my_public_target\");\n    assertThat(rule).isNotNull();\n    assertThat(rule.containsErrors()).isFalse();\n    assertThat(rule.getVisibility().getDeclaredLabels())\n        .containsExactly(RuleVisibility.PUBLIC_LABEL);\n  }\n\n  /** Test 6: A valid rule name is accepted without errors. */\n  @Test\n  public void testValidRuleName() throws Exception {\n    scratch.file(\n        \"pkg/BUILD\",\n        \"\"\"\n        load(\"//rules:my_rule.bzl\", \"my_rule\")\n\n        my_rule(\n            name = \"valid_rule_name\",\n            out = \"output.txt\",\n        )\n        \"\"\");\n\n    Rule rule = (Rule) getTarget(\"//pkg:valid_rule_name\");\n    assertThat(rule).isNotNull();\n    assertThat(rule.getName()).isEqualTo(\"valid_rule_name\");\n    assertThat(rule.containsErrors()).isFalse();\n  }\n\n  /** Test 7: An invalid rule name (containing ':') produces an error. */\n  @Test\n  public void testInvalidRuleName() throws Exception {\n    reporter.removeHandler(failFastHandler);\n    scratch.file(\n        \"pkg/BUILD\",\n        \"\"\"\n        load(\"//rules:my_rule.bzl\", \"my_rule\")\n\n        my_rule(name = \"invalid:name\", out = \"output.txt\")\n        \"\"\");\n\n    Package pkg = loadPackage(\"pkg\");\n    assertThat(pkg.containsErrors()).isTrue();\n    assertContainsEvent(\"target names may not contain ':'\");\n  }\n}\n",

package com.google.devtools.build.lib.packages;
